}






function
google_ad_request_done(google_ads)
{




window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Faith_Hill';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"hill,faith,_,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Faith
Hill</b>
(born
<b>Audrey
Faith
Perry</b>;
September
21,
1967)
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Country_pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
pop">country
pop</a>
singer
and
occasional
actress.
She
is
married
to
country
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
McGraw">Tim
McGraw</a>,
with
whom
she
has
recorded
several
successful
duets.
Hill
has
sold
more
than
40
million
records
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Hill's
first
two
albums,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Take_Me_as_I_Am_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Take
Me
as
I
Am
(Faith
Hill
album)">Take
Me
as
I
Am</a></i>
(1993)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/It_Matters_to_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Matters
to
Me">It
Matters
to
Me</a></i>
(1995),
established
her
as
a
popular
country
singer.
The
pair
placed
a
combined
three
No.
1's
on
Billboard's
country
charts
and
each
received
multi-platinum
certifications
in
the
U.S.
But
the
release
of
her
next
two
albums,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Faith_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Faith
(Faith
Hill
album)">Faith</a></i>
(1998)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Breathe_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breathe
(Faith
Hill
album)">Breathe</a></i>
(1999),
brought
Hill
<a
href="/wiki/Mainstream?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream">mainstream</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crossover
(music)">crossover</a>
and
international
success,
by
achieving
high
positions
and
huge
sales
globally.
<i>Faith</i>
spawned
her
first
international
hit,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Kiss_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Kiss
(Faith
Hill
song)">This
Kiss</a>&quot;,
and
went
multi-platinum
in
various
countries.
<i>Breathe</i>
became
her
best-selling
album
to
date
and
one
of
the
best-selling
country
albums
of
all
time,
by
being
buoyed
by
the
huge
crossover
success
of
her
best
known
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Breathe_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breathe
(Faith
Hill
song)">Breathe</a>&quot;.
It
went
multi-platinum
in
several
countries
around
the
world
and
earned
Hill
three
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Country
Album">Best
Country
Album</a>.
In
2001,
she
recorded
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/There_You%27ll_Be?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
You'll
Be">There
You'll
Be</a>&quot;
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pearl
Harbor
(film)">Pearl
Harbor</a></i>
soundtrack
and
the
song
became
an
international
success
and
her
best-selling
single
in
Europe.
Hill's
next
two
albums,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cry
(Faith
Hill
album)">Cry</a></i>
(2002)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fireflies_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fireflies
(Faith
Hill
album)">Fireflies</a></i>
(2005),
kept
her
mainstream
popularity.
The
former
went
multi-platinum
and
spawned
another
crossover
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cry
(Faith
Hill
song)">Cry</a>&quot;,
which
won
Hill
a
Grammy
Award.
The
latter
went
multi-platinum
as
well,
bolstered
by
the
success
of
the
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mississippi_Girl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mississippi
Girl">Mississippi
Girl</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Like_We_Never_Loved_at_All?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Like
We
Never
Loved
at
All">Like
We
Never
Loved
at
All</a>&quot;,
which
earned
her
another
Grammy
Award.</p>








<p>Hill
has
won
five
Grammy
Awards,
14
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards">Academy
of

Awards</a>,
four
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>
and
several
other
awards.
Her
<a
href="/wiki/Soul2Soul_II_Tour_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006"
class="mw-redirect">Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006</a>
with
McGraw
became
the
highest-grossing

tour
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-soul2_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-soul2-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2001,
she
was
named
one
of
the
&quot;30
Most
Powerful
Women
in
America&quot;
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ladies_Home_Journal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ladies
Home
Journal"
class="mw-redirect">Ladies
Home
Journal</a></i>.
In
2009,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i>
named
her
as
the
No.&nbsp;1
Adult
Contemporary
artist
of
the
2000
decade
and
also
as
the
39th
best
artist.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Hill
was,
from
2007
to
2012,
the
voice
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NBC

Football">NBC
Sunday

Football</a>'</i>s
intro
song.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

breakthrough</a></td>













</tr>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life_and_career_start">Early
life
and
career
start</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life
and
career
start">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Hill
was
born
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ridgeland,_Mississippi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ridgeland,
Mississippi">Ridgeland,
Mississippi</a>,
north
of
<a
href="/wiki/Jackson,_Mississippi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jackson,
Mississippi">Jackson,
Mississippi</a>.
She
was
<a
href="/wiki/Adopted?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adopted"
class="mw-redirect">adopted</a>
as
an
infant,
and
named
Audrey
Faith
Perry.
She
was
raised
in
the
nearby
town
of
<a
href="/wiki/Star,_Mississippi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Star,
Mississippi">Star</a>,
25
miles
outside
of
Jackson,
Mississippi.<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
adoptive
parents,
Edna
and
Ted
Perry,<sup
id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
raised
their
two
biological
sons
along
with
Hill
in
a
devout
<a
href="/wiki/Christian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christian">Christian</a>
environment.<sup
id="cite_ref-king_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-king-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Hill's
vocal
talent
was
apparent
early,
and
she
had
her
first
public
performance,
a
<a
href="/wiki/4-H?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="4-H">4-H</a>
luncheon,
when
she
was
seven.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1976,
a
few
days
before
her
9th
birthday,
she
attended
a
concert
by
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>
at
the
State
Fair
Coliseum,
in
Jackson,
which
impressed
her
deeply.
By
the
time
she
was
a
teenager,
Hill
was
a
regular
performer
at
area
churches,
even
those
not
in
her
own
<a
href="/wiki/Baptist?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baptist"
class="mw-redirect">Baptist</a>
denomination.<sup
id="cite_ref-selfmagazine_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-selfmagazine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
17,
Hill
formed
a
band
that
played
in
local
rodeos.
She
briefly
attended
college
at
<a
href="/wiki/Hinds_Community_College?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hinds
Community
College">Hinds
Community
College</a>
in
Raymond,
Mississippi,
where
she
served
with
a
group
called
the
Hinds
Connection
(a
student
recruiting
and
public
relations
group).
At
times,
she
sang
for
prisoners
at
the
Hinds
County
Jail,
her
song
of
choice
being
&quot;Amazing
Grace&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
age
19
she
quit
school
to
move
to
Nashville
and
pursue
her
dream
of
being
a
country
singer.
In
her
early
days
in
Nashville,
Hill
auditioned
to
be
a
backup
singer
for
<a
href="/wiki/Reba_McEntire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reba
McEntire">Reba
McEntire</a>,
but
failed
to
secure
the
job.<sup
id="cite_ref-king_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-king-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
a
stint
selling
T-shirts,
Hill
became
a
secretary
at
a
music
publishing
firm.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Additionally,
Hill
also
landed
a
job
at
a
local
<a
href="/wiki/McDonald%27s?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>
restaurant
franchise,
which
she
disliked
intensely.
&quot;Fries,
burgers,
cash
register
â€“
I
did
it
all,
I
hated
it,&quot;
she
has
said.<sup
id="cite_ref-Tasteofcountry.com_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Tasteofcountry.com-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1988,
she
married
music
publishing
executive
Daniel
Hill
(not
to
be
confused
with
Canadian
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Dan_Hill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dan
Hill">Dan
Hill</a>).<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Two
years
later,
she
began
a
search
for
her
biological
mother,
whom
she
eventually
met
in
1993
and
with
whom
she
corresponded
until
her
mother's
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-PeopleBio_7-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-PeopleBio-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-biography_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-biography-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
co-worker
heard
Hill
singing
to
herself
one
day,
and
soon
the
head
of
her
music
publishing
company
was
encouraging
her
to
become
a
demo
singer
for
the
firm.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
supplemented
this
work
by
singing
backup
vocals
for
songwriter
Gary
Burr,
who
often
performed
his
new
songs
at
Nashville's
<a
href="/wiki/Bluebird_Cafe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bluebird
Cafe">Bluebird
Cafe</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
one
of
those
performances,
Bob
Saporiti,
an
executive
from
<a
href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warner
Bros.
Records">Warner
Bros.
Records</a>
was
in
the
audience,
and,
impressed
with
Hill's
voice,
began
the
process
of
signing
her
to
a
recording
contract.<sup
id="cite_ref-king_8-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-king-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Shortly
after
the
release
of
her
album,
Hill
found
her
marriage
falling
apart.
She
and
Daniel
Hill
divorced
in
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-biography_14-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-biography-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1993.E2.80.931997:_Country_success">1993â€“1997:
Country
success</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1993â€“1997:
Country
success">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Hill's
debut
album
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Take_Me_as_I_Am_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Take
Me
as
I
Am
(Faith
Hill
album)">Take
Me
as
I
Am</a></i>
(1993);
sales
were
strong,
buoyed
by
the
chart
success
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wild_One_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wild
One
(Faith
Hill
song)">Wild
One</a>&quot;.
Hill
became
the
first
female
country
singer
in
30
years
to
hold
<i>Billboard</i><span
style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s
number
one
position
for
four
consecutive
weeks
when
&quot;Wild
One&quot;
managed
the
feat
in
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-neal_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-neal-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
version
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Piece_of_My_Heart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Piece
of
My
Heart">Piece
of
My
Heart</a>&quot;,
also
went
to
the
top
of
the
country
charts
in
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
sold
a
total
of
3
million
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
Other
singles
from
the
album
include
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Take_Me_as_I_Am_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Take
Me
as
I
Am
(Faith
Hill
song)">Take
Me
as
I
Am</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>The
recording
of
Faith's
second
album
was
delayed
by
surgery
to
repair
a
ruptured
blood
vessel
on
her
<a
href="/wiki/Vocal_cords?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vocal
cords"
class="mw-redirect">vocal
cords</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/It_Matters_to_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Matters
to
Me">It
Matters
to
Me</a></i>
finally
appeared
in
1995
and
was
another
success,
with
the
title
track
becoming
her
fourth
number-one
country
single.
Several
other
top
10
singles
followed,
and
more
than
3
million
copies
of
the
album
were
sold.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
fifth
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Can%27t_Do_That_Anymore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Can't
Do
That
Anymore">I
Can't
Do
That
Anymore</a>&quot;,
was
written
by
country
music
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Alan_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alan
Jackson">Alan
Jackson</a>.
Other
singles
from
the
album
include
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Can%27t_Lose_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Can't
Lose
Me">You
Can't
Lose
Me</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Someone_Else%27s_Dream?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Someone
Else's
Dream">Someone
Else's
Dream</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let%27s_Go_to_Vegas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let's
Go
to
Vegas">Let's
Go
to
Vegas</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>In
spring
1996,
Hill
began
the
Spontaneous
Combustion
Tour
with
country
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
McGraw">Tim
McGraw</a>.
At
that
time,
Hill
had
recently
become
engaged
to
her
former
producer,
<a
href="/wiki/Scott_Hendricks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scott
Hendricks">Scott
Hendricks</a>,
and
McGraw
had
recently
broken
an
engagement.
McGraw
and
Hill
were
quickly
attracted
to
each
other
and
began
an
affair.
After
discovering
that
Hill
was
pregnant
with
their
first
child,
the
couple
married
on
October
6,
1996.
The
couple
have
three
daughters
together:
Gracie
Katherine
(b.
1997),
Maggie
Elizabeth
(b.
1998)
and
Audrey
Caroline
(b.
2001).
Since
their
marriage,
Hill
and
McGraw
have
endeavored
never
to
be
apart
for
more
than
three
consecutive
days.<sup
id="cite_ref-king_8-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-king-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
the
release
of
<i>It
Matters
to
Me</i>,
Hill
took
a
three-year
break
from
recording
to
give
herself
a
rest
from
four
years
of
touring
and
to
begin
a
family
with
McGraw.
During
her
break,
she
joined
forces
with
her
husband
for
their
first
duet,
&quot;It's
Your
Love&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-wix_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wix-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
stayed
at
number
one
for
six
weeks,<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
won
awards
from
both
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music">Academy
of
Country
Music</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Association">Country
Music
Association</a>.
Hill
has
remarked
that
sometimes
when
they
perform
the
song
together,
&quot;it
[doesn't]
feel
like
anybody
else
was
really
watching.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-wix_18-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wix-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1998.E2.80.932003:_Pop_crossover_breakthrough">1998â€“2003:
Pop
crossover
breakthrough</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1998â€“2003:
Pop
crossover
breakthrough">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>She
reentered
the
music
business
in
1998
with
<i>Faith</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-wix_18-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wix-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
showcased
her
progression
toward
a
more
mainstream,
pop-oriented
sound,
although
it
retained
some
country
sound.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Kiss_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Kiss
(Faith
Hill
song)">This
Kiss</a>&quot;
became
a
number
one
country
hit,
and
was
the
first
of
her
singles
to
place
on
the
pop
charts,
peaking
at
number
seven.
More
than
six
million
copies
of
the
album
were
sold.
The
album
also
delivered
several
other
hits
including
another
duet
with
McGraw,
&quot;Just
To
Hear
You
Say
That
You
Love
Me&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Let_Me_Let_Go?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
Me
Let
Go">Let
Me
Let
Go</a>&quot;
and
&quot;The
Secret
of
Life&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>To
follow
up
this
newfound
success,
Hill
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Breathe_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breathe
(Faith
Hill
album)">Breathe</a></i>
in
November
1999,
which
debuted
at
the
top
of
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Country
and
all
genre
charts,
ahead
of
albums
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Savage_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Savage
Garden">Savage
Garden</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-orr_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-orr-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
the
album
had
few
overt
country
sounds,
it
&quot;complement[ed]
her
vocal
strengths.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-dinoia_20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-dinoia-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
the
first
time,
the
album
consisted
solely
of
songs
about
love
and
did
not
venture
into
the
more
somber
territory
that
her
previous
albums
had
touched.<sup
id="cite_ref-dinoia_20-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-dinoia-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
title
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Breathe_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breathe
(Faith
Hill
song)">Breathe</a>&quot;,
reached
number
two
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-orr_19-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-orr-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Way_You_Love_Me_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Way
You
Love
Me
(Faith
Hill
song)">The
Way
You
Love
Me</a>&quot;
hit
the
top
10
as
well,
topping
out
at
number
six
on
the
charts.
The
album
won
Hill
three
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>
including
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Country
Album">Best
Country
Album</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Collaboration_with_Vocals?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Country
Collaboration
with
Vocals">Best
Country
Collaboration
With
Vocals</a>
for
&quot;Let's
Make
Love&quot;
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
McGraw">Tim
McGraw</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Country_Vocal_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Female
Country
Vocal
Performance">Best
Country
Female
Vocal
Performance</a>
for
&quot;Breathe.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
also
marked
a
step
away
from
her
girl-next-door
image,
as
the
videos
and
promotional
pictures
all
portrayed
a
much
sexier
image.
<i>Breathe</i>
has
sold
almost
10
million
copies
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-willman_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-willman-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>2000
was
an
especially
busy
year
for
Hill.
Besides
a
successful
<a
href="/wiki/Soul2Soul_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul2Soul
Tour">tour</a>
with
her
husband,
Hill
was
featured
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/CBS?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CBS">CBS</a>
television
special,
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>'s
<i>Behind
the
Music</i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/VH1_Divas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1
Divas">VH1
Divas
2000</a></i>,
and
the
Lifetime
cable
channel's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Intimate_Portrait_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Intimate
Portrait
(TV
series)">Intimate
Portrait</a></i>
series.<sup
id="cite_ref-orr_19-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-orr-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
She
signed
an
endorsement
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/CoverGirl_(brand)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CoverGirl
(brand)"
class="mw-redirect">CoverGirl</a>
makeup,<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
Awards">Academy
Awards</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>,
appeared
on
the
cover
of
numerous
magazines,
and
performed
the
national
anthem
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Bowl">Super
Bowl</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-orr_19-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-orr-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Hill
was
also
named
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mr._Blackwell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mr.
Blackwell"
class="mw-redirect">Mr.
Blackwell</a>'s
10-best
dressed
women
of
2000,
the
only
singer
listed
among
actresses
and
other
celebrities.
Hill
and
McGraw
also
embarked
on
their
first
Soul2Soul
tour,
the
&quot;Soul2Soul
Tour
2000.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-2000bestdressed_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2000bestdressed-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Musically,
in
2000,
Hill
recorded
a
song
for
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dr._Seuss%27_How_the_Grinch_Stole_Christmas_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dr.
Seuss'
How
the
Grinch
Stole
Christmas
(film)">Dr.
Seuss'
How
the
Grinch
Stole
Christmas</a></i>,
entitled
&quot;Where
Are
You
Christmas.&quot;
The
song
also
appeared
on
the
pop
and
country
charts.
Hill's
success
on
the
pop
charts
disturbed
some
country
music
insiders,
who
questioned
whether
she
was
trying
to
dismiss
her
country
roots
and
move
into
the
pop
genre.
Despite
the
grumbling,
Hill
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/CMA_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMA
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">CMA
Female
Vocalist
of
the
Year
Award</a>,
and
in
her
acceptance
speech
announced,
&quot;I
love
this
business,
and
I
love
this
industry...
and
my
heart
is
here.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-orr_19-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-orr-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2001,
Hill
recorded
a
song
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pearl
Harbor
(film)">Pearl
Harbor</a></i>
soundtrack
which
was
originally
offered
to
<a
href="/wiki/Celine_Dion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Celine
Dion">Celine
Dion</a>.
It
is
one
of
her
most
critically
acclaimed
song.
Besides,
as
how
she
said
it
in
her
own
words,
&quot;One
of
the
biggest
honor
of
my
career
is
being
asked
to
sing
a
theme
from
Pearl
Harbor.&quot;<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(February
2014)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/There_You%27ll_Be?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
You'll
Be">There
You'll
Be</a>&quot;
also
appeared
on
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/There_You%27ll_Be_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="There
You'll
Be
(album)">There
You'll
Be:
The
Best
of
Faith
Hill</a></i>,
an
international
greatest
hits
album.
The
album
featured
dance
mixes
of
&quot;Breathe&quot;
and
&quot;The
Way
You
Love
Me&quot;
along
with
alternate
versions
of
&quot;Piece
of
My
Heart&quot;
and
&quot;Let
Me
Let
Go.&quot;
&quot;There
You'll
Be&quot;
is
considered
to
be
Hill's
biggest
hit
single
in
the
UK
up
to
date.
The
song
was
nominated
for
a
2002
Grammy
Awards
for
Best
Female
Pop
Vocal
Performance
and
for
an
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
Award
for
Best
Original
Song">Academy
Award
for
Best
Original
Song</a>.</p>








<p>In
2002,
Hill
released
her
new
album
with
a
more
pop-oriented
sound,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cry
(Faith
Hill
album)">Cry</a></i>.
The
album
&quot;spotlight[ed]
her
impressive
set
of
pipes,&quot;
but
also
marked
the
completion
of
her
&quot;transformation
into
a
pop
diva,&quot;
containing
few
nods
to
her
country
roots.
Though
the
album
debuted
at
number
one
on
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
magazine"
class="mw-redirect">Billboard
magazine</a>'s
pop
and
country
album
charts,<sup
id="cite_ref-huey_9-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-huey-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Hill
made
her
debut
as
musical
guest
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saturday
Night
Live">Saturday
Night
Live</a></i>,
the
album's
singles
(including
the
title
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cry
(Faith
Hill
song)">Cry</a>&quot;,
written
and
originally
performed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Angie_Aparo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angie
Aparo">Angie
Aparo</a>)
received
much
less
radio
airplay
than
her
previous
smashes.<sup
id="cite_ref-silberman_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-silberman-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
however,
did
win
a
Grammy
Award
and
3.7
million
copies
have
been
sold
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-grammy_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-grammy-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Hill's
2002
song
&quot;Baby
You
Belong&quot;
off
her
<i>Cry</i>
album
was
used
as
the
theme
song
for
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Lilo_%26_Stitch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lilo
&amp;
Stitch">Lilo
&amp;
Stitch</a></i>.
The
music
video
featured
clips
from
the
movie
as
well
as
performance
clips.</p>

In
concert
in

on
the











<a

<p>In
2005,
Hill
returned
with
her
new
country
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fireflies_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fireflies
(Faith
Hill
album)">Fireflies</a></i>.
The
CD
debuted
on
top
of
the
Billboard
Country
and
all
genre
album
charts,
placing
her
among
only
a
handful
of
artists
to
have
three
consecutive
albums
debut
at
number
one
on
both
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-firefliescmt_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-firefliescmt-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
debut
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Mississippi_Girl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mississippi
Girl">Mississippi
Girl</a>&quot;,
became
Hill's
highest-debuting
single.
The
song
was
written
specifically
for
her
by
<a
href="/wiki/John_Rich_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Rich
(musician)"
class="mw-redirect">John
Rich</a>
(of
<a
href="/wiki/Big_and_Rich?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
and
Rich"
class="mw-redirect">Big
and
Rich</a>)
and
Adam
Shoenfield
of
<a
href="/wiki/MuzikMafia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MuzikMafia">MuzikMafia</a>,
and
tells
the
abbreviated
story
of
her
life.
Hill
recorded
two
other
songs
by
Rich,
&quot;Sunshine
and
Summertime&quot;
and
&quot;Like
We
Never
Loved
at
All&quot;,
both
of
which
became
successful
singles.<sup
id="cite_ref-cook_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cook-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
title
track,
&quot;Stealing
Kisses&quot;
and
&quot;If
You
Ask&quot;
were
written
by
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Lori_McKenna?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lori
McKenna">Lori
McKenna</a>
and
also
appear
on
McKenna's
albums.
The
album
marked
a
return
to
Hill's
country
roots
and
succeeded
in
reestablishing
her
place
on
country
radio.<sup
id="cite_ref-nucountry_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nucountry-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2006,
after
a
six-year
break
from
touring
following
the
birth
of
her
youngest
daughter,<sup
id="cite_ref-king_8-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-king-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
Hill
and
husband
Tim
McGraw
embarked
on
their
<a
href="/wiki/Soul2Soul_II_Tour_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006"
class="mw-redirect">Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006</a>.
The
tour
became
the
highest
grossing
country
music
tour
ever
with
a
gross
of
$90
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-soul2_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-soul2-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-barker_28-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-barker-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
named
&quot;Major
Tour
of
the
Year&quot;
by
the
prestigious
Pollstar,
beating
out
such
heavyweights
as
<a
href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2007.E2.80.932010:_The_Hits.2C_Joy_to_the_World_and_Sunday_Night_Football">2007â€“2010:
The
Hits,
Joy
to
the
World
and
Sunday
Night
Football</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
2007â€“2010:
The
Hits,
Joy
to
the
World
and
Sunday
Night
Football">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2007,
Hill
started
work
on
her
first
domestic
greatest
hits
package,
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Hits_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Hits
(Faith
Hill
album)">The
Hits</a></i>,
which
was
released
on
October
2.
It
contains
two
new
tracks,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lost_(Faith_Hill_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost
(Faith
Hill
song)">Lost</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Red_Umbrella?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Red
Umbrella">Red
Umbrella</a>&quot;,
as
well
as
13
additional
tracks.
The
album
also
features
hits
covering
her
entire
career
from
1993â€“2005.
Included
with
the
2-Disc
Special-Edition
of
<i>The
Hits</i>
is
a
DVD
of
11
of
Hill's
music
videos.
The
DVD
substitutes
the
Tim
McGraw
duet
&quot;Just
To
Hear
You
Say
That
You
Love
Me&quot;
for
their
&quot;I
Need
You&quot;
duet
on
the
CD.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>She's
also
featured
on
husband
Tim
McGraw's
2007
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Let_It_Go_(Tim_McGraw_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Let
It
Go
(Tim
McGraw
album)">Let
It
Go</a></i>.
She
sings
two
duets
with
him,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Need_You_(2007_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Need
You
(2007
song)"
class="mw-redirect">I
Need
You</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Shotgun
Rider.&quot;
Both
songs
were
sung
at
the
couple's
critically
acclaimed
<a
href="/wiki/Soul2Soul_II_Tour_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006"
class="mw-redirect">Soul2Soul
II
Tour
2006</a>.
She
and
Tim
also
did
an
encore
of
their
Soul2Soul
II
Tour;
<a
href="/wiki/Soul2Soul_2007?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soul2Soul
2007"
class="mw-redirect">Soul2Soul
2007</a>
began
in
June
and
ran
through
August.
The
song
<i>I
Need
You</i>
has
been
nominated
twice
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50th
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2008
Grammy
Awards</a>
for
<i>Best
Country
Collaboration
with
Vocals</i>
and
<i>Best
Country
Song</i>.
The
show
took
place
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Staples_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Staples
Center">Staples
Center</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Los
Angeles">Los
Angeles</a>,
CA
on
February
10,
2008
but
the
song
didn't
win.</p>








<p>In
2007,
Hill
took
over
as
the
signature
voice
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/NFL_on_NBC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NFL
on
NBC">NFL
on
NBC</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NBC
Sunday
Night
Football">Sunday
Night
Football</a></i>,
singing
the
theme
song
about
which
the
show's
producer
said:<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<blockquote
class="templatequote">









<p>It's
not
often
that
you
get
the
opportunity
to
have
a
mega-star
like
Faith
Hill
perform
the
signature
open
to
your
show.</p>









<div
class="templatequotecite">









â€”NBC
Sunday
Night
Football
producer
Fred
Gaudelli,&nbsp;









<cite><i>MSNBC</i></cite>








</div>








</blockquote>








<p>Hill
performed
the
opening
theme
until
April
15,
2013,
when
she
announced
that
she
will
no
longer
sing
the
intro
for
<i>Sunday
Night
Football</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
September
2008,
Hill
issued
her
first
Christmas
album,
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Joy_to_the_World_(Faith_Hill_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joy
to
the
World
(Faith
Hill
album)">Joy
to
the
World</a></i>.
The
compilation
was
given
positive
reviews,
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/About.com?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="About.com">about.com</a></i>,
which
gave
the
album
four
and
a
half
out
of
five
stars,
calling
the
album,
&quot;a
great
collection
of
classic
Christmas
songs&quot;.
Hill
continually
worked
on
the
album
two
years
prior
to
its
official
release.
The
album
included
one
new
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/A_Baby_Changes_Everything?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Baby
Changes
Everything">A
Baby
Changes
Everything</a>&quot;,
which
was
released
as
the
album's
only
single
in
late
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;24
on
Billboard's
AC
chart,
and
quickly
rose
to
No.&nbsp;1,
becoming
Hill's
fourth
number
one
on
that
chart.</p>








<p>On
February
1,
2009,
Hill
performed
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/America_the_Beautiful?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="America
the
Beautiful">America
the
Beautiful</a>&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLIII?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Bowl
XLIII">Super
Bowl
XLIII</a>
pregame
show.
The
other
performers
at
the
pregame
show
were
<a
href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jennifer
Hudson">Jennifer
Hudson</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Journey_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Journey
(band)">Journey</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Springsteen">Bruce
Springsteen</a>
performed
at
the
Halftime
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
2010,
Hill
contributed
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Country_Strong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Strong">Country
Strong</a></i>
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Strong_(soundtrack)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Strong
(soundtrack)">soundtrack</a>.
On
it,
she
recorded
a
song
titled
'Give
in
to
Me'.
Hill
also
appears
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Coal_Miner%27s_Daughter:_A_Tribute_To_Loretta_Lynn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coal
Miner's
Daughter:
A
Tribute
To
Loretta
Lynn"
class="mw-redirect">Coal
Miner's
Daughter:
A
Tribute
To
Loretta
Lynn</a></i>,
on
which
she
performs
&quot;Love
Is
The
Foundation&quot;.
Hill
also
contributed
her
vocals
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ryan_Tedder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ryan
Tedder">Ryan
Tedder</a></i>
penned
song
&quot;All
I
Ever
Wanted&quot;
for
the
2010
feature
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Life_as_We_Know_It_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Life
as
We
Know
It
(film)">Life
As
We
Know
It</a></i>.
The
song
was
used
in
trailers
to
promote
the
film
and
also
appeared
during
the
end
credits
of
the
film.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="2011.E2.80.93present:_New_studio_album">2011â€“present:
New
studio
album</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
2011â€“present:
New
studio
album">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Brendan
O'Brien,
known
for
producing
projects
for
Bruce
Springsteen,
Pearl
Jam,
and
Rage
Against
the
Machine,
is
working
with
Hill
and
producing
her
next
album,
originally
set
for
release
in
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Hill
entered
the
studio
with
pop
producer
Brian
Kennedy
in
January
2011
to
complete
the
album.</p>








<p>In
March
2011,
Hill
returned
to
the
studio
for
another
round
of
recording.
&quot;I
would
like
to
have
a
record
out,&quot;
Hill
told
Billboard.com,
&quot;but
it
hasn't
been
the
right
thing
yet.
I
don't
want
it
to
be
just
another
record.
It's
a
lot
of
work
to
support
a
record,
so
I
just
want
it
to
be
...
really
great.
I
want
it
to
represent
where
I
am
as
a
woman.
I
don't
want
it
to
be
fake.
I
want
it
to
be
authentic
and
real.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
mid-2011,
Hill
recorded
a
duet
with
<a
href="/wiki/George_Strait?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Strait">George
Strait</a>
on
the
song
&quot;A
Showman's
Life&quot;
which
can
be
heard
on
Strait's
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Here_for_a_Good_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Here
for
a
Good
Time">Here
for
a
Good
Time</a></i>.</p>








<p>Hill
performed
the
album's
first
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Come_Home_(OneRepublic_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Come
Home
(OneRepublic
song)">Come
Home</a>&quot;,
on
the
CMA
Awards
on
November
9,
2011.</p>








<p>On
September
17,
2012,
Hill
debuted
the
song
&quot;Illusion&quot;
during
a
performance,
filmed
in
June
2012,
on
<a
href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Broadcasting
Company">ABC</a>'s
coverage
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/CMA_Music_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMA
Music
Festival">CMA
Music
Festival</a>.
Hill
confirmed
the
album
was
done,
but
made
no
comment
about
when
it
would
be
released
or
whether
the
rumored
title
of
<i>Illusion</i>
was
official.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
new
single,
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/American_Heart_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Heart
(song)">American
Heart</a>&quot;,
was
released
on
October
1,
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2012,
Faith
Hill
and
Tim
McGraw
began
a
20-show
run
of
their
Soul2Soul
show
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_Venetian_Las_Vegas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Venetian
Las
Vegas">Venetian</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Las
Vegas
Valley">Las
Vegas</a>.
A
second
leg
of
the
show
will
run
from
October
2013
to
April
2014.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"

ventures</span>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Acting_career">Acting
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Acting
career">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1995,
Hill
guest
starred
in
an
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Touched_by_an_Angel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touched
by
an
Angel">Touched
by
an
Angel</a></i>.
Hill
won
the
role
of
<a
href="/wiki/Julia_Compton_Moore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Julia
Compton
Moore">Julia
Compton
Moore</a>,
the
wife
of
LTC
<a
href="/wiki/Hal_Moore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hal
Moore">Hal
Moore</a>,
played
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mel_Gibson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mel
Gibson">Mel
Gibson</a>,
in
the
2002
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/We_Were_Soldiers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We
Were
Soldiers">We
Were
Soldiers</a></i>
but
ultimately
left
the
film,
giving
the
role
to
<a
href="/wiki/Madeline_Stowe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madeline
Stowe"
class="mw-redirect">Madeline
Stowe</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Tasteofcountry.com_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Tasteofcountry.com-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
Her
film
debut
was
in
the
summer
of
2004,
when
Hill
co-starred
with
<a
href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nicole
Kidman">Nicole
Kidman</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Matthew_Broderick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matthew
Broderick">Matthew
Broderick</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Glenn_Close?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glenn
Close">Glenn
Close</a>
in
director
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Oz?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Oz">Frank
Oz</a>'s
remake
of
the
1975
thriller
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Stepford_Wives_(2004_movie)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Stepford
Wives
(2004
movie)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Stepford
Wives</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-susman_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-susman-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
Although
the
film
earned
over
$101
million,
it
was
savaged
by
critics<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Hill
has
not
made
another
acting
appearance
since.
While
hers
was
a
small
part,
she
provided
one
of
the
more
talked
about
scenes
with
a
scream
that
made
Tim
McGraw
proud.<sup
id="cite_ref-Tasteofcountry.com_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Tasteofcountry.com-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Fragrance">Fragrance</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Fragrance">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
October
2009,
Hill
released
her
first
fragrance
titled
<i>Faith
Hill
Parfums</i>.
The
fragrance
is
a
blend
of
Southern
Magnolia,
Jasmine
and
Peach
Pears.
In
2010,
Hill
released
her
second
fragrance,
titled
<i>True</i>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Philanthropy">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Hill
used
her
1999
tour
to
support
a
national
children's
book
drive,
The
Faith
Hill
Family
Literacy
Project.
The
charity
was
inspired
by
Faith's
father,
who
faced
challenges
with
literacy.
Fans
who
donated
books
at
one
of
her
concerts
were
entered
into
a
drawing
to
meet
her
personally
after
the
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-book_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-book-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
effort
resulted
in
the
donation
of
35,000
children's
books,
which
were
distributed
to
hospitals,
schools,
libraries,
and
daycare
centers
in
40
cities
across
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-bookrecap_43-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bookrecap-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
days
immediately
following
<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Katrina">Hurricane
Katrina</a>,
Hill
and
her
husband,
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
McGraw">Tim
McGraw</a>,
who
was
raised
in
<a
href="/wiki/Louisiana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>,
joined
groups
taking
supplies
to
<a
href="/wiki/Gulfport,_Mississippi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gulfport,
Mississippi">Gulfport,
Mississippi</a>.
The
two
also
hosted
several
charity
concerts
to
benefit
those
who
were
displaced
by
the
storm.<sup
id="cite_ref-abcnews_44-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-abcnews-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
Later
in
the
year
the
couple
established
the
Neighbor's
Keeper
Foundation,
which
provides
funding
for
community
charities
to
assist
with
basic
humanitarian
services
in
the
event
of
a
natural
disaster
or
for
desperate
personal
circumstances.
In
a
special
gesture,
the
couple
also
donated
profits
from
their
performance
in
<a
href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Orleans,
Louisiana"
class="mw-redirect">New
Orleans</a>
to
<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Katrina">Hurricane
Katrina</a>
relief.<sup
id="cite_ref-katrina_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-katrina-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
June
2010,
Hill,
along
with
her
husband
Tim
McGraw,
organized
Nashville
Rising,
a
benefit
concert
aimed
to
raise
$2
million
for
The
Community
Foundation
of
Middle
Tennessee
in
response
to
the
flood
in
early
May
that
killed
22
people
and
caused
$2
billion
in
damage.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h3><span

awarded
annually
by
the

of
Recording
Arts
and
Sciences">National
Academy
of
Recording
Arts
and
Sciences</a>.
Hill
has
won
5
awards
from
15
nominations</p>

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Other_awards">Other
awards</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Faith_Hill&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
Other
awards">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
addition
to
her
5
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>,
Hill
has
also
won
12
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards">Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards</a>,
4
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>,
4
<a
href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People's
Choice
Awards">People's
Choice
Awards</a>,
3
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Association
Awards">Country
Music
Association
Awards</a>,
among
others.<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition,
Hill
received
the
Samuel
S.
Beard
Award
for
Greatest
Public
Service
by
an
Individual
35
Years
or
Under
in
2000,
an
award
given
out
annually
by&nbsp;<a
href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jefferson
Awards
for
Public

Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a

type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Faith_Hill&page=1&ac=24&qid=774468A299B9299B369F2BC5DC57843B&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();
